        gptSubPage = window.digitalData && digitalData.page && digitalData.page.subPage ? digitalData.page.subPage : "blank";

        function gptClean(gptText) {
            if (typeof (gptText) == "string") {
                gptText = gptText.replace(/\&/g, '%26');
                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="91a2669be1194b709ccd12b8c99701fd">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'e87f36b4-fcad-4592-b225-f2c666421928'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d32965227" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Transition metal sulfides (TMSs) still confront the challenges of capacity fading and inferior fast-charging capability for sodium storage. The rational design of heterostructures enables a new approach to conquer these drawbacks. In this work, a hierarchical structure consisting of SnS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets and FeS<sub>2</sub> microrods with triphasic heterostructures is proposed by the facile secondary growth and sulfidation process. The introduction of tin sources regulates the proportion of pyrite and marcasite phases, thereby achieving the triphasic heterostructures comprising pyrite, marcasite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>. When served as anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the optimized sample exhibits a high reversible capacity (901&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>) and durable cycling performances (827&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> and 742&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 700 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>). Paring with the commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathodes, the full-cell also delivers extraordinary cyclic stability with a high capacity of 618&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> (based on the weight of anode material) after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> (98.7% capacity retention). The hierarchical structure with adjustably triphasic heterogeneous interfaces alleviates the volumetric expansion and interfacial passivation of active material, while modulating the energy band structure and inducing the build-in electric fields to boost Na<sup>+</sup>/electrons transport rate.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314679-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314679-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have emerged as a highly promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), due to the abundant sodium resource and similar operated mechanism.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0001_R_d32965212e511" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Science">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0003_R_d32965212e511" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the stability and lifespan of SIBs are always limited by the sluggish reaction kinetics, which are caused by the large sodium ion radius. The commercial graphite anode for LIBs cannot be translated into the SIBs system directly, owing to its inadequate layer spacing for accommodating the repeated insertion of Na<sup>+</sup>. Therefore, seeking the ideal anode material is still crucial for the development of advanced SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0004_R_d32965212e518" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nano Energy">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0005_R_d32965212e518" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - ACS Nano">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Transition metal sulfides (TMSs) with insertion and conversion sodium storage mechanisms have garnered significant attention, due to their strong competitiveness of high specific capacity, low-cost, moderate metal-sulfur bond, and redox reversibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0006_R_d32965212e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - ACS Nano">6</a>-<a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0009_R_d32965212e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Nano-Micro. lett.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As the representative of these TMSs, FeS<sub>2</sub> with high theoretical capacity (894&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>), low price, and nontoxicity would be suitable for sodium storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0010_R_d32965212e534" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Mater. Chem. A">10</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0011_R_d32965212e534" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - J. Mater. Chem. A">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, capacity fading, pulverization, structural degeneration, and poor rate performance caused by the combined effect of large volume expansion and intrinsically low electrical conductivity are still impossible to ignore.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0012_R_d32965212e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Energy Environ. Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Rational structural engineering composited with a bifunctional carbon matrix has served as a certified and common route to improve the electrochemical performances of FeS<sub>2</sub> anode. For example, a metalorganic framework (MOF) derived FeS<sub>2</sub>@C exhibits an improved rate and cyclic performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0013_R_d32965212e551" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Electrochim. Acta">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The regular arrangement of metal-ligands units in MOF precursor facilitates the subsequent preparation of uniformly carbon-coated metal sulfides composites. In addition, the construction of the heterostructures comprising binary or multiple metallic sulfides also delivers improved sodium storage performances. The hetero-interface incorporated various components would increase the active reaction sites to enhance the ion storage properties. Moreover, the induced build-in electric field (BEF) by <i>n</i>-/<i>p</i>-type semiconductor interface accelerates the electron transport, thereby increasing the rate performances of anode materials. CuS/FeS<sub>2</sub>@NC nanocube delivers a remarkable long-term cycle life with 99.1% capacity retention at the end of 300 cycles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0014_R_d32965212e563" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Small">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The incorporation of alloy-type storage mechanism components (the compounds of Sn and Sb) for constructing heterostructure is regarded as an efficient route to enhance the specific capacity and of iron sulfides-based anode. FeS<sub>1-x</sub>/SnS@C heterostructure has proved beneficial for the cyclic stability and rapid sodium diffusion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0015_R_d32965212e571" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J Power Sources">15</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0016_R_d32965212e571" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Chem. Eng. J.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub>@FeS<sub>2</sub> heterostructure with an N-doped graphene matrix exhibits 85.7% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 5&nbsp;Ag<sup>1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0017_R_d32965212e585" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - ACS Nano">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Layered tin disulfide (SnS<sub>2</sub>) with a large interlayer distance favors the reversible sodium ions intercalation/extraction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0018_R_d32965212e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Chem. Eng. J.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, the BEF induced by FeS<sub>2</sub> (<i>p</i>-type) and SnS<sub>2</sub> (<i>n</i>-type) semiconductor interface further enhances the application potential of FeS<sub>2</sub>/SnS<sub>2</sub> composited materials. SnS<sub>2</sub>/FeS<sub>2</sub>@rGO heterostructure bonded by covalence shows a superior rate capability of 429.6&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> at 6&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0018_R_d32965212e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Chem. Eng. J.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>However, the heterojunction interfaces would be gradually passivated by the repeated and asynchronous conversion/alloyingdealloying processes. The soluble intermediate reaction products are still weakening the reaction kinetics at the same time. Fortunately, the generation of triphasic or multiphasic heterogeneous interfaces would induce more active sites and optimize the electronic structure to suppress the passivation process synergistically.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0019_R_d32965212e626" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Appl. Catal. B-Environ.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, owing to the similar formation energy of pyrite and marcasite phases, the as-prepared FeS<sub>2</sub> would exhibit a natural heterogeneous interface. However, the co-existence phenomenon of pyrite and marcasite has been overlooked, due to the decreasing crystallinity (affected by the carbon matrix) and adjacent/overlapped diffraction peaks of the two types FeS<sub>2</sub>. Notably, pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> with a cubic structure usually delivers a better electrochemical performance than that of orthorhombic marcasite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0020_R_d32965212e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Chem. Eng. J.">20</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0021_R_d32965212e638" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Thus, it is urgent to construct a rational structure to improve the electrochemical performances of FeS<sub>2</sub>-based anode by a comprehensive consideration of the heterostructure effect and the proportion of the marcasite phase.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, the triphasic heterostructures consisting of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>, marcasite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> have been constructed through the secondary growth route on the surface of MIL-88A precursor combining with the sulfidation process (<b>Scheme</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0007">1</a>). The strategy of secondary growth on the MOF precursor surface ensures an abundance of contact sites between iron and tin sources, thereby facilitating the formation of heterogeneous interfaces. Interestingly, the presence of tin in the FeS<sub>2</sub> structure reduces the formation energy of pyrite phase and inhibits the formation trend of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>, synchronously. By adjusting the amount of tin sources, the three types of heterogeneous interfaces with triphasic structures can be achieved (the sample obtained by the optimized ratio is denoted as FFS-TH). When served as anode material for SIBs, the FFS-TH electrode exhibits superior electrochemical performances compared to its counterparts (pyrite/marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub> biphasic heterostructures, pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>/SnS<sub>2</sub> biphasic heterostructures and bare SnS<sub>2</sub>), including the high reversible capacity of 901&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with 82.7% initial coulombic efficiency, stable cyclic and rate retention of 827&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> and 742&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 700 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. Furthermore, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH full coin cell displays a high capacity of 618&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with 98.7% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7a5424aa-3aa0-4437-bf9e-8ab9b92506e4/adfm202314679-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7a5424aa-3aa0-4437-bf9e-8ab9b92506e4/adfm202314679-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4ae06aa2-84a3-48cf-bc3a-225ee472a422/adfm202314679-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7a5424aa-3aa0-4437-bf9e-8ab9b92506e4/adfm202314679-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

                  </div>

               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314679-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314679-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>The morphological and structural features of as-prepared samples are first characterized by scanning electron microscope (SEM) and transmission electron microscope (TEM). As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1a,b</a>, FF-BH presents a microrods-like morphology with 510&nbsp;m in length and 300500&nbsp;nm in diameter, intact inheriting the morphology of Fe-MOF precursor (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1a</a>, Supporting Information). The rough and tight surface would be attributed to the growth of primary particles and carbonization of organic ligands during the sulfidation process. The TEM image of FF-BH depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1c</a> reveals solid microrod morphology, confirming the SEM results. There are two clear sets of lattice fringes with the spacing of 0.24 and 0.34&nbsp;nm in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1d</a>, which belonged to the crystal plane of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> (210) and marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub> (110), respectively. Considering of the obvious adjacent grain boundaries, FF-BH would be regarded as a heterostructure comprising pyrite and marcasite phases. After secondary growth, amorphous SnO<sub>2</sub> particles are formed on both the surface of the rod and within the gap between adjacent rods (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1b</a>, Supporting Information). Affected by the SnO<sub>2</sub> deposition, the morphology of FFS-TH exhibits typical hierarchical morphology consisting of 1D rod and 2D nanosheets (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1e,f</a>), which significant differences compared to that of FF-BH. The length of the FFS-TH microrod is similar to its counterpart. However, the 1D mircorod assembled from numerous primary particles delivers the hollow structure with a porous surface, which would be attributed to the etching during the secondary growth process in the weakly alkaline environment. In addition, the formation and growth of nanosheets destroy partial hollow microrods, thereby increasing the proportion of heterogeneous interfaces between FeS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>. These structural features are further represented by the TEM. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1g</a>, there are several nanosheets laying vertically and flatly on the microrods to construct the hierarchical structure. At the junction of nanosheet and microrod, the flat nanosheet traverses the plane to form a clear grain boundary (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1h</a>). The well-identified lattice fringes in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1i</a> are simulated from the enlarged area I, II, and III (in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0001">1h</a>) by fast Fourier transform to represent the crystal plane spacing clearly. As a result, these lattice fringes with the distances of 0.59, 0.20, and 0.31&nbsp;nm are assigned to the lattice plane of SnS<sub>2</sub> (001), pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> (210), and marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub> (111), respectively, demonstrating the formation of triphasic heterostructures to enrich the heterogeneous interfaces. Such a hierarchical structure with triphasic heterostructures would not only moderate the volumetric expansion, but also accelerate the diffusion of sodium ions and electrons. Energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDX) elemental mapping images of this region display the uniform Fe, Sn, S, and C distribution, indicating the numerous existences of heterogeneous interfaces.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/253520b8-0980-4ea0-b4af-e804a0f0a622/adfm202314679-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/253520b8-0980-4ea0-b4af-e804a0f0a622/adfm202314679-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f2d83de5-932d-40c8-8dd9-fbee27e014d0/adfm202314679-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/253520b8-0980-4ea0-b4af-e804a0f0a622/adfm202314679-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) SEM, c) TEM and d) HRTEM images of FF-BH, ef) SEM, g) TEM and h) HRTEM images of FFS-TH; i) FFS-TH lattice fringes simulated from the marked area by fast Fourier transform; j) EDX elemental mapping images of FFS-TH.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>As the counterpart, FS-BH prepared by excessive tin source addition also display the hierarchical structure consisting of nanosheets and microrods, which is similar to FFS-TH, except for the increased amount and thickness of nanosheets (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1ce</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the HRTEM image of FS-BH presents two distinct and adjacent sets of lattice fringes with interplanar spacing of 0.27 and 0.59&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (200) crystal plane of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> and (001) crystal plane of hexagonal SnS<sub>2</sub>, respectively, which is the main evidence for the existence of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>/SnS<sub>2</sub> biphasic heterostructures in FS-BH (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1f</a>, Supporting Information). In the absence of the Fe-MOF template, the SS (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1g,h</a>, Supporting Information) exhibits a larger and thicker sheet morphology with a diameter of 210&nbsp;m and thickness of 300600&nbsp;nm, in comparison to FFS-TH and FS-BH. BrunauerEmmettTeller (BET) method is further utilized to evaluate the impact of Sn addition on the specific surface area (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). The specific surface area of FFS-TH (59.67&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>) is much higher than that of FF-BH (15.68&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>) and FS-BH (37.69&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>). This enhanced specific surface area of FFS-BH compared with FF-BH is attributed to the stack and growth of nanosheets on the microrods surface. However, with the increasing of Sn addition, the larger and thicker SnS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets would superfluously extrude and destroy the microrods, which caused the formation of stacked macropores, and finally reduced the specific surface area and electrochemical active of FS-BH.</p>
         
         <p>The phase compositions of the as-prepared samples are identified by X-ray diffraction (XRD). As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2a</a>, all the diffraction peaks of FF-BH can be clearly assigned to pyrite and marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub> with joint committee on power diffraction standards (JCPDS) numbers of 421340 and 370475, respectively. The pattern of SS displays the standard diffraction peaks without any impurity phases, assigning to the hexagonal SnS<sub>2</sub> (JCPDS: 230677). After the addition of the tin source, FFS-TH shows an inconspicuous triphasic structures consisting of SnS<sub>2</sub>, pyrite, and marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>. It is worth noting that the diffraction peak of (110) crystal plane located at 26 has almost disappeared, which is an indication of the decreased content of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>. With the increasing of tin source addition, the decreasing trend of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub> content in FS-BH becomes more pronounced. Besides, the evolution of diffraction peaks in the enlarged area also reveals this interesting phenomenon, indicating that the presence of a tin atom suppresses the formation of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>. Furthermore, this speculation is supported by the analysis of the X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) spectrum. In Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2b</a>, the high-resolution Fe 2p spectrum of FFS-TH would revealed multiple components. In detail, the fitted peaks located at 707.1, 708.6, 710.2, 712.4, 716.3, 719.9, 724.1, 725.8, and 733.1&nbsp;eV could be assigned to the marcasite Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, marcasite Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> (corresponding oxidation states), Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, Sn 3p<sub>3/2</sub>, marcasite Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, Fe<sup>3+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>, and corresponding satellite peak, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0014_R_d32965212e902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Small">14</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0022_R_d32965212e902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">22</a>-<a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0024_R_d32965212e902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Significantly, as the characteristic peaks of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>, the intensity of Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Fe<sup>2+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub> peaks visibly decrease from FF-BH to FS-BH, which is affected by the variation in tin source addition during the preparation processes. Additionally, the overlapped Fe 2p and Sn 3p signals are detected to reveal the co-existence heterointerfaces between pyrite, marcasite, and SnS<sub>2</sub> at the surface of FFS-TH and FS-BH.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0025_R_d32965212e920" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem. Eng. J.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> All of the high-resolution Sn 3d spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2c</a>) can be divided into four peaks corresponding to the Sn<sup>2+</sup> 3d<sub>5/2</sub>, Sn<sup>4+</sup> 3d<sub>5/2</sub>, Sn<sup>2+</sup> 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, and Sn<sup>4+</sup> 3d<sub>3/2</sub>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0026_R_d32965212e946" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Front Mater Sci">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The formation of low-valence tin would be attributed to the reduction effect of the carbon layer during the sulfidation process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0027_R_d32965212e952" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Molecules">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> S 2p peaks have closely spaced spin-orbit components composed by S 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and S 2p<sub>1/2</sub> with a gap of about 1.16&nbsp;eV. The S 2p spectrum of FFS-TH depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2d</a> is composed of metal-sulfur bonds (FeS and SnS bonds were distinguished), CS bonds and absorbed sulfur oxide groups, suggesting a strong chemical bonding to improve the conductivity of carbon matrix.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0025_R_d32965212e964" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem. Eng. J.">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0028_R_d32965212e964" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - ACS Nano">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The presence of S-doped carbon is further confirmed by C 1s spectrum of FFS-TH. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2e</a>, three fitted peaks can be clearly observed, assigning to CC, CS, and CO bond, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0029_R_d32965212e973" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Phys. Chem. C">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cc1f15dc-3030-40cc-ac4c-de6e70855221/adfm202314679-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/cc1f15dc-3030-40cc-ac4c-de6e70855221/adfm202314679-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/83e3c79e-6535-434d-b09e-d3dca502dfee/adfm202314679-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cc1f15dc-3030-40cc-ac4c-de6e70855221/adfm202314679-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns, b) Fe 2p and c) Sn 3d high-resolution spectra of as-prepared samples; d) S 2p and e) C 1s high-resolution spectrum of FFS-TH; <sup>57</sup>Fe Mssbauer spectra of FF-BH, FFS-TH and FS-BH.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The carbon matrix structure of FFS-TH is elucidated by Raman spectroscopy. In the Raman spectrum of FFS-TH, the divided peaks at 1320 and 1540&nbsp;cm<sup>1</sup> would be assigned to defects carbon (D-band), graphitic carbon (G-band), respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3a</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0030_R_d32965212e1008" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Electrochim. Acta.">30</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0031_R_d32965212e1008" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - CrystEngComm">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The additional peak at 1440&nbsp;cm<sup>1</sup> caused by atomic vibration of SnS<sub>2</sub> is also observed in FS-BH (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3b</a>, Supporting Information) and SS (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3d</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0032_R_d32965212e1024" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Mater. Res. Bull.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, the value of <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> is about 0.96 calculated from the intensity ratio of D-band and G-band peak, further revealing the graphitic carbon layer to improve the conductivity of FFS-TH anode. Furthermore, a TG test is carried out to determine the carbon content of FFS-TH. During the heating treatment in the air atmosphere, it would undergo the oxidation of ferrous, conversion of metal sulfides to oxide, and combustion of carbon matrix, successively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). After the determination of the atomic ratio of Fe: Sn (4.56: 1) by inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometer (ICP-OES), combined with the total weight loss (39.08%), the carbon content can be calculated as 7.5&nbsp;wt.%. The <sup>57</sup>Fe Mssbauer spectra are further performed to reveal the evolution of phase composition. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0002">2f</a>, the spectrum of FF-BH can be fitted to three hyperfine doublets with the isomer shift (IS) of 0.40, 0.52, and 1.37&nbsp;mm&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> and quadrupole splitting (QS) of 0.57, 0.69 and 2.51&nbsp;mm&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup>, which are corresponding to the Fe<sup>2+</sup> in pyrite, marcasite, and FeS<i><sub>x</sub></i>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0033_R_d32965212e1054" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Alloy. Compd.">33</a>-<a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0036_R_d32965212e1054" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The phase ratio of pyrite and marcasite is 1.06:1 in FF-BH composite. Impressively, this ratio rises to 1.61 and 3.07 in FFS-TH and FS-BH, respectively, which further confirmed the evolution of FeS<sub>2</sub> phase by the tin induction. It's worth noting that the difference result in the content of the marcasite phase between Mssbauer and XPS spectra would be caused by their different detection depths. According to the variation in the formation energies of pyrite and marcasite by density functional theory (DFT) calculation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), the preference for formation has been reversed from marcasite to pyrite by the result of tin addition, which confirmed the inhibitory effect of tin on marcasite phase theoretically. Excessive addition of tin inhibits the formation of the marcasite phase on the surface, and finally constructs a pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>/SnS<sub>2</sub> biphasic heterostructures.</p>
         
         <p>Moreover, the model of triphasic heterostructures comprising pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>, marcasite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and hexagonal SnS<sub>2</sub> is presented to reveal the influences of these unique structural features on sodium storage performances (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0003">3a</a>). The partial density of states (DOS) of marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>, pyrite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and hexagonal SnS<sub>2</sub> all exhibit an obvious band gap near the Fermi level (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6ac</a>, Supporting Information). Impressively, the DOS of constructed biphasic (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6d,e</a>, Supporting Information) and triphasic heterostructures (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0003">3b</a>) presents the continuous electron distribution, indicating metallic characteristics to improve their electronic conductivity than bare FeS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>. The high density of states of FFS-TH at the Fermi level means the potential of accelerated electron/ion transfer. Besides, FFS-TH also delivers a smallest average electrical resistivity (4.04&nbsp;&nbsp;cm) than that of FF-BH (11.91&nbsp;&nbsp;cm) and FS-BH (20.52&nbsp;&nbsp;cm), which is in agreement with theoretical calculation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the difference in charge density of triphasic heterostructures reveals the imbalanced charge distribution between triphasic interfaces, which induced the formation of a build-in electric field to promote the Na<sup>+</sup>/electron transfer and the reaction kinetics. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>, marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>, hexagonal SnS<sub>2,</sub> and triphasic heterostructures are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0003">3d</a>. The lowest energy barrier of triphasic heterostructures demonstrates that the presence of a build-in electric field between triphasic interfaces would partly promote the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the electrode material. However, the electrochemical performance of as-prepared materials in assembled cells needs to undergo a comprehensive evaluation.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/14edf23b-596f-4a2e-87b0-b85ab9cb5ec6/adfm202314679-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/14edf23b-596f-4a2e-87b0-b85ab9cb5ec6/adfm202314679-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e80fd9f3-d6a8-4a4b-9f05-fd1c54f4390f/adfm202314679-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/14edf23b-596f-4a2e-87b0-b85ab9cb5ec6/adfm202314679-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) the structural model, b) partial density of states and c) difference charge density of triphasic heterostructures; d) Na<sup>+</sup> migration energy of pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>, marcasite FeS<sub>2</sub>, hexagonal SnS<sub>2</sub>, and triphasic heterostructures.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>A series of electrochemical evaluations through the CR2032 half-cells are carried out to assess the sodium storage performances of as-prepared samples. The first four cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of FFS-TH in the potential range of 0.0052.5&nbsp;V at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> are depicted in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4a</a> to reveal the sodiation and desodiation processes during the initial cycles. In the first sodiation process, the sharp cathodic peak at about 1.2&nbsp;V is a result of Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation into FeS<sub>2</sub> crystal to form Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> (0&nbsp;&lt;&nbsp;x&nbsp; 2).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0037_R_d32965212e1173" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J Power Sources">37</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0038_R_d32965212e1173" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - ACS Nano">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The subsequent peaks would be attributed to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation reaction of SnS<sub>2</sub> (0.67&nbsp;V), the formation of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI, 0.5&nbsp;V),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0039_R_d32965212e1183" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Alloy. Compd.">39</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0040_R_d32965212e1183" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - J. Alloy. Compd.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the further conversion and alloying reaction of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub> and metallic Sn to form metallic Fe, Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>Sn and Na<sub>2</sub>S (at low potential),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0040_R_d32965212e1199" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - J. Alloy. Compd.">40</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0041_R_d32965212e1199" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> respectively. Besides, the cathodic peak at 0.05&nbsp;V and anodic peak at 0.08&nbsp;V are characteristic of the solvated Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/deintercalation into carbon matrix in the ether-based electrolyte. The broad anodic peaks 0.2 and 1.3&nbsp;V are associated with the dealloy reaction of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>Sn and desodiation process of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub>, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0039_R_d32965212e1215" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Alloy. Compd.">39</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0042_R_d32965212e1215" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Chem. Eng. J.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, the overlapping CV curves after the first cycle indicate the reliable reversibility and stability of FFS-TH. Compared with the CV curves of other counterparts (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8ac</a>, Supporting Information), FFS-TH anode encompasses the sodium storage process of FeS<sub>2</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>, which can be considered as the superposition of their characteristic peaks. The broad and mild peaks in FFS-TH and FS-BH would be attributed to the accelerated redox processes by the influence of heterogeneous interfaces.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4db169d7-edd3-46a3-828d-25037d4f944f/adfm202314679-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4db169d7-edd3-46a3-828d-25037d4f944f/adfm202314679-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8ae8663d-be07-47b0-99ad-d6b47cab7c8f/adfm202314679-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4db169d7-edd3-46a3-828d-25037d4f944f/adfm202314679-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves at 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> and b) initial chargedischarge curves at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> of FFS-TH; c) cyclic performances at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>; d) rate performances; e) long-term cyclic evaluation of FFS-TH at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>; f) comparison of electrochemical performances between FFS-TH and reported iron sulfides-based anodes; h) GITT curves and i) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient at different states of FF-BH, FFS-TH, and FS-BH.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4b</a>, the FFS-TH anode delivers the discharge and charge capacity of 1090 and 901&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>, respectively, with an initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 82.7%, which is highest among the as-prepared samples ( 78.6% of FF-BH, 80.5% of FS-BH and 52.7% of SS, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8df</a>, Supporting Information). The enhanced ICE can be attributed to the well-constructed triphasic heterostructures, which accelerated the charge transfer and mitigated the irreversible the side-reactions. The enhanced ICE of FFS-TH would be attributed to the triphasic heterostructure and the suitable specific surface area, which facilitated the electrons/ions transfer to improve the electrode reactivity and provides numerous active sites for participation in the desodiation reaction to mitigate the irreversible the side-reactions, respectively. Moreover, the well-overlapping dischargecharge curves after the first discharge of FFS-TH demonstrate superior reversibility compared to its counterparts. In the cyclic evaluation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4c</a>), FFS-TH exhibits the highest retentive discharge capacity (827&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>) than all the counterparts (586, 778, and 227&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> of FS, FS-BH, and SS, respectively) after 200 cycles under a current density of 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. Moreover, FFS-TH combines the advantages of FeS<sub>2</sub> (cyclic stability) and SnS<sub>2</sub> (high theoretical capacity), showing a stable cyclic performance with high reversible capacity after the activation stage. The low capacity of SS would be ascribed to large volumetric expansion during the alloyingdealloying process, which resulted in the pulverization and deactivation of SnS<sub>2</sub> particles. All the Nyquist plots of as-prepared electrodes after 100 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> display the semicircle in the high-frequency region and a line in the low-frequency region (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information). Clearly, the lowest charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) of FFS-TH electrode (2.15&nbsp;), indicates its best capability for charge transfer (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). Besides, the FFS-TH also displays the best rate performances among the as-prepared samples, which can be well restored after the high current density.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0043_R_d32965212e1296" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nanoscale">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4d</a>, the reversible capacity of FFS-TH at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> is 884, 868, 902, 894, 867, 750, and 946&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>, respectively. Moreover, FFS-TH exhibits a stable voltage plateau at different current densities, indicating its fast and stable sodium storage capability (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). Notably, the FFS-TH cell maintains a reversible capacity of 742&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with close to 100% coulombic efficiency after 700 monotonous cycles under 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4e</a>). The capacity fluctuations between the 150250 cycles would be affected by the change of test temperature. Moreover, the stable and overlapped voltage plateau at different cycles indicates the regular sodiation/desodiation reaction without accompanying side-reaction during the cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information). These excellent electrochemical performances of FFS-TH are superior to the reported iron/tin sulfides-based composite electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0017_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - ACS Nano">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0018_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Chem. Eng. J.">18</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0021_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">21</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0037_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J Power Sources">37</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0044_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Mater. Chem. C">44</a>-<a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0054_R_d32965212e1326" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - J. Materiomics">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) methods are carried out to evaluate the sodium ions diffusion ability in the as-prepared electrodes during the discharge and charge processes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0055_R_d32965212e1333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Adv. Sci.">55</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0056_R_d32965212e1333" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Chem. Eng. J.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4h</a>, the voltage-time curves of as-prepared electrodes are similar to their corresponding dischargecharge curves. According to the Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202314679-disp-0001" title="Link to equation">1</a>), the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) at different states is calculated and depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0004">4i</a> (the meaning of the parameters can be referred to in our previous works).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0055_R_d32965212e1353" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Adv. Sci.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To summarize, the values of D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> change dynamically with the different discharge/charge of depth. The lower D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of FFS-TH in some potential ranges would be imputed to the adsorption of Na<sup>+</sup> by the strong BEF (induced by triphasic heterojunction) and electrical double layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0057_R_d32965212e1367" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Adv. Energy Mater.">57</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0058_R_d32965212e1367" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - J Electrochem Soc">58</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the triphasic heterostructure and induced BEF contribute positively to the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion on the whole. As a result, the comprehensive D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> of FFS-TH surpasses that of FF-BH and FS-BH, which is always in the range of 10<sup>12</sup>10<sup>10</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> with no obvious low values.

            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202314679-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/c327e75c-c309-4f99-96eb-536e7c351974/adfm202314679-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202314679:adfm202314679-math-0001" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202314679-math-0001.png">

                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">Additionally, the charge storage mechanism is studied by CV with different scan rates to further ascertain the reason for the superior rate performance of FFS-TH electrode. The CV curves of FFS-TH display a similar and enlarged shape with the increasing scanning rate (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0005">5a</a>). The whole charge storage consists of diffusion-controlled and pseudocapacitive contributions. Based on the Equation&nbsp;(<a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#adfm202314679-disp-0002" title="Link to equation">2</a>), the pseudocapacitive contribution would be estimated.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0059_R_d32965212e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Rare Met.">59</a>, <a href="#adfm202314679-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202314679-bib-0060_R_d32965212e1458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Chem. Eng. J.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202314679-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/800edc89-4ddb-47ae-ac51-621b07f04d41/adfm202314679-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202314679:adfm202314679-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202314679-math-0002.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>i</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>k</mi>
                              <mn>1</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <mi>v</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>k</mi>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mn>0.5</mn>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}i = {k}_1v + {k}_2{v}^{0.5}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6d0afabe-645b-4597-a92d-9ef32532130f/adfm202314679-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/6d0afabe-645b-4597-a92d-9ef32532130f/adfm202314679-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8f3683d6-c25a-470e-ad35-a95b129e3150/adfm202314679-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6d0afabe-645b-4597-a92d-9ef32532130f/adfm202314679-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of FFS-TH at different scanning rates; b) pseudocapacitive contribution of FFS-TH at 1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup>; c) comparison of pseudocapacitive contribution at different scanning rates.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0005">5b</a>, the whole area of the CV curve at 1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> represents the whole stored charge of FFS-TH electrode. The red region depicted by the values of <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> corresponds to the pseudocapacitive contribution. As the result, the pseudocapacitive contribution of FFS-TH at 1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>1</sup> is estimated to 91.4%, which is the highest among the all as-prepared electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0005">5c</a>, the CV curves of FF-BH, FS-BH, and SS at different scanning rate are depicted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). The original and dominated pseudocapacitive contribution of FFS-TH induced by hierarchical structure and triphasic interfaces would be considered as the critical reason for its superior rate performances.</p>
         
         <p>Moreover, the cells after 50 cycles were dissected to verify the FFS-TH structural stability. Clearly, the hierarchical morphology consisting of microrods and nanosheets can be observed in the SEM and TEM images of cycled electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a,b</a>, Supporting Information). The HRTEM image of cycled FFS-TH (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13c</a>, Supporting Information) delivers the obvious several sets of lattice fringes, corresponding to pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub>, marcasite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub>, respectively, which demonstrated the stability of triphasic interfaces. In addition, the cross-section SEM images of pristine and cycled electrode of FFS-TH (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13d</a>, Supporting Information) exhibit only 10.5% increase in thickness, which is much lower than that of FF-BH (53.2%, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13e</a>, Supporting Information) and FS-BH (75.7%, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13f</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that the as-prepared hierarchical structure with moderated SnS<sub>2</sub> coating endows the electrode with an excellent ability to accommodate the volumetric expansion during the cycles.</p>
         
         <p>To evaluate the potential of FFS-TH in practical applications, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH coin full cells are assembled with the commercial Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0006">6a</a>). The specific capacity of full cells is calculated based on the mass of FFS-TH anode. According to the voltage plateau of active materials, the full cells are operated in the voltage range of 0.83.4&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0006">6b</a>). As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0006">6c</a>, the full cell displays a high capacity of 618&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with 98.7% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. Moreover, the as-prepared full cell delivers superior rate performances with a specific capacity of 719, 711, 672, 627, 557, 343, and 690&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and back to 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0006">6d</a>). Impressively, after the rate evaluation, Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH still exhibits the stable cyclic property with a capacity of 211&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> (68% capacity retention) after 965 cycles at a high current density of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. Combined with the obvious voltage plateaus (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202314679-fig-0006">6e</a>) at different current densities, Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH would be expected to work in some electronic devices.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202314679-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4d3910c6-021f-465a-9d07-bee9d43ca48c/adfm202314679-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4d3910c6-021f-465a-9d07-bee9d43ca48c/adfm202314679-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ce494719-38af-4697-959a-d7a3ad4a9606/adfm202314679-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4d3910c6-021f-465a-9d07-bee9d43ca48c/adfm202314679-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202314679-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202314679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of full-cell; b) chargedischarge curves of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH coin full cell; The c) cyclic performance and d) rate performance and chargedischarge curves at different current densities of the full cell.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202314679-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202314679-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, the engineering of triphasic nanostructures consisting of pyrite, marcasite FeS<sub>2,</sub> and SnS<sub>2</sub> as high-capacity, ultrastable, and fast-charging anode material has been presented through a secondary growth and sulfidation process. The introduction of SnS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets not only constructs a hierarchical structure with FeS<sub>2</sub> microrods to alleviate the volumetric expansion and increase the active sites for charge storage, but also regulates the proportion of pyrite and marcasite phases to optimize the triphasic heterostructures. As the result of triphasic interfaces, the induced build-in electric field promotes the reversibility of the conversion-alloying processes and facilitates the Na<sup>+</sup>/electrons transfer. Moreover, more heterogeneous interfaces in triphasic heterostructures alleviate the interfacial passivation and maintain the interfacial electrochemical activity. The optimized FeS<sub>2</sub>/SnS<sub>2</sub> triphasic nanostructures (FFS-TH) deliver a high reversible capacity of 901&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with 82.7% ICE, superior cyclic stability of 827&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> and 742&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> after 700 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> and excellent rate performance of 750&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. Furthermore, the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>FFS-TH full coin cell displays a high capacity of 618&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup> with 98.7% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>1</sup>. The regulable construction of triphasic heterostructure provides a new approach to achieve ideal anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
